樂典格蓋西神神主之眞乎此一蠻
與善物薺名雨而之木而原聖家山
禮遠類音作盡遺念偶詞文教無貝
並惡苟之原斯其油莠能尤詩分府
重而得道爲爲貌然靈工當歌畛光
也不其咸吾得尤而毫者追之威怪
斯自道人教之不生無若其所雖陸
編知必最頌然可哉生譯神由西離
所此能深主而泥是氣者味譯國目
載古使上之難其以焉失蓋也之不
聖諷可需矣貌譯能其文夫珍暇
上王誦以雖是而詩感髓生譯何給
帝之之通然編失者發液於詩妨因
造治者神余所其固人徒情之作思
生天默明更譯神不心存未道東聖
之下化下有多必可使皮有固方會
德所潛可望係也慕其毛情當之原
基以移以焉泰形其愛猶不本用屬

例曹
一 1 1
吾教曩用之頌主聖詩原係艾約瑟理一視二先生所譯原詩計二百六
十六一章今删去三十九章重譯者二十薏新增者二百二章餘俱俅原文
更正共得四百二十九章
是編中有中西友人所I〗所作者皆載其名於本章之下免致湮沒
括編所課悉本原交然泰西文法迥異中土譯之之時必當理其次序順
其語氣務使神理畢呈未敢刻舟求劍閭有用中華典故成語者大抵以
其適近擷文未敢勉强金合雖似乎優孟衣冠難免貽譏大雅然被之佾
偷律呂庶幾有咸同心
是編所譯重乎神味蓋詩本性情語忌腐板愦之所至能以通乎神明格
於上下編中所載凡上主之慈恩聖徒之忠愛以及天人交感 ie際身世
變遷之懷莫不追神慕態以期觸目愴懷庶使詠之者有以貢具讃頌之
P興其敬 愛 之 <1
i 俗 未 必 I 通 文義是 編純以 淺俗 耳v文取其易解然淺而忌乎泛
俗而避乎鄙以期雅俗共賞觸目了然其間成偶用不甚通俗之字大抵
爲韻所限耳


是編所譯之詩多#名作其原詩隹處如天造地設稍一移易便失元神
而中西文法叉多 $ 者
求自然謹避艱滥間有語句較生者 ★ 抵或係西國成語或係聖糙故實
乍見似覺眢解久用自必圓通
是編用韻皆本於五方元音非第取其寛也緣詩韻平聲雖分上下未判
陰陽如一東之東同一先之先賢之類又有同在一韻北方讀 取
音者如支\支窺十三元之元尊等類故斯編悉遵元音間有未然者或
爲原文听限或爲袼調所枸讀者諒之
聖詩原爲講之樂鞏以便歌詠其字句之輕重必合音節之抑楊大柢實
字多重虛罕多輕要字多重間字多輕如我的二字則我重的輕可喜二
字則可輕而真：重也餘可類推
是編除總目外另有細目以每節首句桉其字畫爲次第如第一二字同
II者則以第三四字爲准以便簡閲
是編中疊句如係特有一調者則疊句附於！節V羧若係能通用常調
者則疊句附於未尾以便去取

求主賜我安息
我心繅能完全
在天蒙主迎接
求安可就我來
將首靠我心懷
寘是憂衰弱
主使我心歡樂
我是生命水泉
生命必承保全
得嘗那泉美味
我今活在主內
我造暗世之光
此光終日厢彰
他逄我日我星
直到世路畢經

第三百二十七暈
我主我王我心最愛

人人心中愛主尊名
長者引領幼者則效
讃主歌聲自屋而 起

LONDON MISSIONARY SOCIETY
TIENTSIN.
1891.


In due time, the Church of Christ in China will bring
itrs own rich strain of melody to swell the Hallelujah Chorus
of a ransomed world. As yet its home -song has hardly
begun, although the following pages could perhaps never
have seen the light without the aid of one who has given to
them one or two lyrics which may help us to imagine what
it shall be. Meanwhile, our Chinese brethren have a valid
claim to share the treasures of sacred song which have been
the fruitage of the Christian centuries in other lands. As we
find help in our Service of Praise in the use of translations
of the noble hymns of Anatolis and Gregory, Luther and
Bernard, so will tens of thousands in China make their own
the sweet hymns of the lands whose sons and daughters
have brought to them the Gospel, if they can be given to
them in fitting To do this in some measure, is the
main purpose of this Volume, which, though far from reaching
its ideal, will it is hoped, bring the Chinese Church Hymnal
of the future at least a step nearer.
Experience has shown that, especially in the case of
the most famous and best loved hymns of the universal
(Church, there is always a strong desire to find reproduced in
a translation every shade of thought and even of expression.
No doubt, if form and spirit can be alike preserved, they
ought to be. This affectionate reverence is a safe guide when
wisely controlled. But it is a difficult task, and full of
dangers. The most literal translation is not necessarily the
best. Natural grace and poetic feeling may have vanished.
Even perspicuity may have been sacrificed to literal accuracy.
Such thoughts have been ever present during the
preparation of this Volume. Most of the translations it
contains have not I think been attempted by others, and
over 200 are now published for the first time. Not a few
of those contained in 詩 頌主聖詩 对 对 77) have been
replaced by closer renderings, while about 40 have been
omitted, and the rest, with a few exceptions, have been


much altered. The exceptions are some hymns from other
hands. As the book is thus practically a new one, it has
received a new name, which does not limit its scope to hymns
of praise. The remark has been made that some of the
hymns are too high in style. Others have been thought to
be too colloquial, Surely there should be variety. Besides,
the subject often decides the style. <c There is a happy land
and 0 Worship the King all glorious above are not equally
simple in English. To make them so in Chinese would be a
mistake, even were it possible. But both should be
intelligible, and the simpler hymn equally with the other,
should not offend a cultivated taste.
I wish here to express my gratitude to God for the
valuable service whicVi my Chinese fellow worker h
has here been permitted to render to the Church. He was
one of my first students, and has for nearly 30 Years been a
faithful helper, but it. is possible that in these pages he has
done the noblest work of his life. It is interesting to recall
that his venerable father was my assistant in the preparation
cf the 頌主聖詩
I desire also to offer warm thanks to many brethren
connected with various Missions, and especially to my own
beloved colleagues, for much helpful suggestion and criticism.
The hope of serving them has been a constant stimulus.
It only remains to say with much regret that distance
and other circumstances have deprived this Volume of the
critical help which my dear old friend Dr. Edkins gave to its
predecessor twenty years ago.
JONATHAN LEES.
Tientsin, June 24th 1891.


NOTE TO NUMERICAL INDEX.
I. In the list given below the date 1862 is attached
to hymns of Dr. J. Edkins and William C. Burns published
in a book so dated, which was the germ of the present
volume. In 1870 • these were revised by Dr. Edkins and
others for the i 頌主聖詩 issued in 1871. They
have now once again been revised.
11. The date 1870 appended to my own hymns for
the collection of 1871 really covers several years. The
later dates are more strictly accurate.
111. For the names and dates of English writers lam
indebted mainly to the admirable u Congregational Church
Hymnal” and the late Fleming Stevenson’s “Hymns for
Church and Home.”
IY. The true first lines of hymns 122, 168, 231, 244
have here been replaced by those of hymns in Mr.
collection which suggested them, to indicate their character.
